2026 CHAPTER 18
===============

An Act to make provision about the supply of tobacco, vapes and other products, including provision prohibiting the sale of tobacco to people born on or after 1 January 2009 and provision about the licensing of retail sales and the registration of retailers; to enable product and information requirements to be imposed in connection with tobacco, vapes and other products; to control the advertising and promotion of tobacco, vapes and other products; and to make provision about smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and heated tobacco\-free places.

\[29th April 2026]

Be it enacted by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—


Part 1Sale and distribution: England and Wales
----------------------------------------------

### Sale of tobacco etc

#### 1Sale of tobacco etc

(1\)It is an offence to sell any of the following to a person born on or after 1 January 2009—


(a)a tobacco product;


(b)a herbal smoking product;


(c)cigarette papers.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1) to prove—


(a)that they took such steps as may be specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State to verify that the customer was born before 1 January 2009, or


(b)that they otherwise took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(3\)Before making regulations under subsection [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1-2)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1-2-a) the Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers if the regulations contain provision which would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if contained in an Act of the Senedd.


(4\)Regulations under subsection [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1-2)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1-2-a) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(5\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I1S. 1 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I2S. 1 in force at 1\.1\.2027 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(3\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/3)

Prospective

#### 2Purchase of tobacco etc on behalf of others

(1\)It is an offence for a person aged 18 or over to buy, or attempt to buy, any of the following on behalf of a person born on or after 1 January 2009—


(a)a tobacco product;


(b)a herbal smoking product;


(c)cigarette papers.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2) to prove that they had no reason to suspect that the other person was born on or after 1 January 2009\.


(3\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2) in respect of cigarette papers to prove that they had no reason to suspect that the other person intended to use the papers for smoking.


(4\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I3S. 2 in force at 1\.1\.2027, see [**s. 175(3\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/3)

Prospective

#### 3Tobacco vending machines

(1\)A person commits an offence if the person has the management or control of premises on which a tobacco vending machine is available for use.


(2\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-3) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


(3\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-3) “tobacco vending machine” means a machine from which any of the following products may be bought or from which they are dispensed to a customer in connection with a sale—


(a)tobacco products,


(b)herbal smoking products, or


(c)cigarette papers.


Commencement Information

I4S. 3 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 4Sale of unpackaged cigarettes

(1\)It is an offence for a tobacco retailer to sell cigarettes that are not in their original packaging.


(2\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-4) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.


(3\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-4) “original packaging” means the retail packaging in which the cigarettes were supplied to the tobacco retailer for the purpose of sale.


Commencement Information

I5S. 4 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 5Age of sale notice at point of sale: England

(1\)A tobacco retailer who sells tobacco products on premises in England must display an age of sale notice on those premises.


(2\)For the purposes of this section an “age of sale notice” is a notice containing the following statement—


 “It is illegal to sell tobacco products to anyone born on or after 1 January 2009”.


 (3\)The notice must be displayed in a prominent position where it is readily visible to people at each point of sale of tobacco products.


(4\)The notice must comply with any requirements set out in regulations made by the Secretary of State as to the size or appearance of—


(a)the statement to be displayed on the notice, or


(b)any other aspect of the notice.


(5\)Regulations under [subsection (4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5-4) are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


(6\)A person who fails to display an age of sale notice as required by [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) commits an offence.


(7\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) to prove that they took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(8\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I6S. 5 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I7S. 5 in force at 1\.1\.2027 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(3\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/3)

#### 6Age of sale notice at point of sale: Wales

(1\)A tobacco retailer who sells tobacco products on premises in Wales must display an age of sale notice on those premises.


(2\)For the purposes of this section an “age of sale notice” is a notice containing both the following statements—


 “It is illegal to sell tobacco products to anyone born on or after 1 January 2009”


 “Mae’n anghyfreithlon gwerthu cynhyrchion tybaco i unrhyw un a anwyd ar neu ar ôl 1 Ionawr 2009”.


 (3\)The notice must be displayed in a prominent position where it is readily visible to people at each point of sale of tobacco products.


(4\)The notice must comply with any requirements set out in regulations made by the Welsh Ministers as to the size or appearance of—


(a)the statement to be displayed on the notice, or


(b)any other aspect of the notice.


(5\)Regulations under [subsection (4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5-4) are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


(6\)A person who fails to display an age of sale notice as required by [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) commits an offence.


(7\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) to prove that they took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(8\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I8S. 6 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I9S. 6 in force at 1\.1\.2027 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(3\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/3)

Prospective

### Snus etc

#### 7Ban on manufacture of snus etc

(1\)It is an offence to manufacture a relevant oral tobacco product.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-8-1) “relevant oral tobacco product” means a tobacco product that—


(a)is intended for oral use,


(b)is not intended to be inhaled or chewed, and


(c)consists wholly or partly of tobacco in powder or particulate form.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—


(a)on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


Commencement Information

I10S. 7 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 8Ban on sales of snus etc

(1\)It is an offence to—


(a)sell a relevant oral tobacco product, or


(b)offer or expose a relevant oral tobacco product for sale.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-8-1) “relevant oral tobacco product” has the meaning given by section [7](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-7)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-7-2).


(3\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to prove that they took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(4\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—


(a)on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


Commencement Information

I11S. 8 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 9Possession of snus etc with intent to supply

(1\)It is an offence for a person to have a relevant oral tobacco product in their possession with intent to supply it to another in the course of business.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-8-1) “relevant oral tobacco product” has the meaning given by section [7](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-7)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-7-2).


(3\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—


(a)on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


Commencement Information

I12S. 9 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Sale of vaping and nicotine products etc

#### 10Sale of vaping or nicotine products to under 18s

(1\)It is an offence to sell a vaping product or nicotine product to a person who is under the age of 18\.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to prove—


(a)that they took such steps as may be specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State to verify that the customer was at least 18 years old, or


(b)that they otherwise took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(3\)Before making regulations under subsection [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10-2)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10-2-a) the Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers if the regulations contain provision which would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if contained in an Act of the Senedd.


(4\)Regulations under subsection [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10-2)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10-2-a) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(5\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I13S. 10 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I14S. 10 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 11Purchase of vaping or nicotine products on behalf of under 18s

(1\)It is an offence for a person aged 18 or over to buy, or attempt to buy, a vaping product or nicotine product on behalf of a person who is under the age of 18\.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2) to prove that they had no reason to suspect that the other person was under the age of 18\.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


Commencement Information

I15S. 11 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 12Vaping and nicotine product vending machines

(1\)A person commits an offence if the person has the management or control of premises on which a vape vending machine or a nicotine product vending machine is available for use.


(2\)But [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-12-1) does not apply in relation to a vape vending machine made available for use in a mental health hospital if the machine is in an area that is intended wholly or mainly for inpatients.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


(4\)In this section—


<ul><li><p>“<span>mental health hospital</span>” means an institution (or part of an institution) maintained wholly or mainly for the reception and treatment of inpatients who—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>are aged 18 or over, and
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>are suffering from mental disorder (within the meaning of the Mental Health Act 1983);
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>nicotine product vending machine</span>” means a machine—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>from which nicotine products may be bought, or
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>from which they are dispensed to a customer in connection with a sale;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>vape vending machine</span>” means a machine—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>from which vaping products may be bought, or
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>from which they are dispensed to a customer in connection with a sale.
</p></div></div></div></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I16S. 12 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Displays of products or prices

#### 13Displays of products or prices in England

(1\)The Secretary of State may by regulations impose prohibitions, requirements or limitations on retailers in relation to—


(a)the display, in the course of business, of relevant products in a place in England where the products are offered for sale;


(b)the display, in the course of business, of empty retail packaging of relevant products in a place in England where the products are offered for sale;


(c)the display, in the course of business, of prices of relevant products in a place in England where the products are offered for sale.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13-1) “relevant products” means—


(a)tobacco products,


(b)tobacco related devices,


(c)herbal smoking products,


(d)cigarette papers,


(e)vaping products, or


(f)nicotine products.


(3\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13-1)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13-1-a) a reference to a product includes anything that represents the product and that is intended to be exchanged for it at the point of sale.


(4\)Regulations under this section may create offences in relation to a failure to comply with the regulations.


(5\)The regulations must provide for any offence to be triable either way and punishable—


(a)on summary conviction, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


(6\)Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must consult any persons the Secretary of State considers it appropriate to consult.


(7\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I17S. 13 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I18S. 13 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 14Displays of products or prices in Wales

(1\)The Welsh Ministers may by regulations impose prohibitions, requirements or limitations on retailers in relation to—


(a)the display, in the course of business, of relevant products in a place in Wales where the products are offered for sale;


(b)the display, in the course of business, of empty retail packaging of relevant products in a place in Wales where the products are offered for sale;


(c)the display, in the course of business, of prices of relevant products in a place in Wales where the products are offered for sale.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13-1) “relevant products” means—


(a)tobacco products,


(b)tobacco related devices,


(c)herbal smoking products,


(d)cigarette papers,


(e)vaping products, or


(f)nicotine products.


(3\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14-1)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14-1-a) a reference to a product includes anything that represents the product and that is intended to be exchanged for it at the point of sale.


(4\)Regulations under this section may create offences in relation to a failure to comply with the regulations.


(5\)The regulations must provide for any offence to be triable either way and punishable—


(a)on summary conviction, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


(6\)Before making regulations under this section the Welsh Ministers must consult any persons they consider it appropriate to consult.


(7\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I19S. 14 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I20S. 14 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Free distribution and discounts

#### 15Free distribution and discount of products

(1\)A person commits an offence if—


(a)the person—


(i)gives away a product or coupon to a member of the public or sells a product or coupon at a substantial discount, or


(ii)causes or permits that to happen, and


(b)either—


(i)their purpose in doing so is to promote a relevant product, or


(ii)the effect of their doing so will be to promote a relevant product and they know, or have reason to suspect, that will be the effect.


(2\)In subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13-1) “relevant product” means—


(a)a tobacco product,


(b)a herbal smoking product,


(c)cigarette papers,


(d)a vaping product, or


(e)a nicotine product.


(3\)Where a person is charged with an offence under this section of giving away a vaping product or nicotine product, or a coupon for such a product, it is a defence for the person to prove that the product or coupon was given away in accordance with arrangements made by a public authority.


(4\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—


(a)on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court, or a fine, or both;


(b)on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years, or a fine, or both.


(5\)In this section “coupon” means anything (whether in physical or electronic form) which, by itself or together with something else, can be redeemed for a product or service or for cash or any other benefit.


Commencement Information

I21S. 15 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Retail licensing: England

#### 16Prohibition of retail sales of tobacco products etc in England without a licence

(1\)An individual must not do any of the following things in England except under the authority of and in accordance with a personal licence—


(a)sell relevant products;


(b)expose relevant products for sale;


(c)possess relevant products for the purpose of their sale (by the individual or another person).


(2\)A person must not use or permit the use of premises in England for any of the following things except under the authority of and in accordance with a premises licence—


(a)the storage of relevant products for the purpose of their sale (by the person or another person);


(b)the exposure of relevant products for sale;


(c)the supply of relevant products to retail customers.


(3\)The Secretary of State may by regulations create exceptions to the prohibition in [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2).


(4\)The Secretary of State must by regulations make provision for and in connection with the grant of personal licences and premises licences.


(5\)Before making regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16) the Secretary of State making them must consult any persons that the Secretary of State considers it appropriate to consult.


(6\)[Schedule 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1) makes further provision about regulations under [subsection (4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-4).


(7\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(8\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes variation or renewal;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-2">paragraph 2</a> of <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1">Schedule 1</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” means a licence that is granted by a licensing authority and authorises an individual to do the things mentioned in <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1">subsection (1)</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1-a">(a)</a>, <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1-b">(b)</a> and <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1-c">(c)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” means a licence that is granted by a licensing authority and authorises the use of premises by a person for the things mentioned in <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2">subsection (2)</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2-a">(a)</a>, <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2-b">(b)</a> and <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2-c">(c)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant products</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>tobacco products;
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>herbal smoking products;
</p></div><div><div>(c)</div><p>cigarette papers;
</p></div><div><div>(d)</div><p>vaping products;
</p></div><div><div>(e)</div><p>nicotine products;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>supply</span>” includes despatch.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I22S. 16 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

Prospective

#### 17Offences in connection with licences: England

(1\)A person who breaches the prohibition in [section 16](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-1) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-2) commits an offence.


(2\)A person commits an offence if—


(a)the person provides information to a licensing authority—


(i)in, or in connection with, an application for the grant of a personal licence or a premises licence, or


(ii)in pursuance of any other obligation imposed by or under regulations made under [section 16](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16)[(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-4),


(b)the information is false or misleading in a material respect, and


(c)the person knows, or ought reasonably to know, that the information is false or misleading in a material respect.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17) is liable on summary conviction to a fine.


(4\)The court by which a person is convicted of an offence under [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17-1) may order the relevant products to which the offence relates, and any container for them, to be forfeited and either destroyed or dealt with in such other manner as the court may order.


(5\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes variation or renewal;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-2">paragraph 2</a> of <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1">Schedule 1</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant product</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I23S. 17 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

#### 18Financial penalties for breach of licence conditions: England

(1\)A local weights and measures authority or relevant district council in England may impose a financial penalty on a person if satisfied that—


(a)the person has breached a condition attached to a personal licence or a premises licence, and


(b)the breach of that condition does not constitute an offence under [section 17](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17).


(2\)The amount of the financial penalty must not exceed £2,500\.


(3\)The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the amount specified in [subsection (2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18-2) for the purpose of reflecting inflation.


(4\)[Schedule 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2) makes further provision about the imposition of financial penalties under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18).


(5\)Regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


(6\)In this section—


<ul><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant district council</span>” means a district council that—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>is specified as a licensing authority under <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-2">paragraph 2</a> of <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1">Schedule 1</a>, and
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>is not a local weights and measures authority.
</p></div></div></div></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I24S. 18 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Retail licensing: Wales

#### 19Prohibition of retail sales of tobacco products etc in Wales without a licence

(1\)An individual must not do any of the following things in Wales except under the authority of and in accordance with a personal licence—


(a)sell relevant products;


(b)expose relevant products for sale;


(c)possess relevant products for the purpose of their sale (by the individual or another person).


(2\)A person must not use or permit the use of premises in Wales for any of the following things except under the authority of and in accordance with a premises licence—


(a)the storage of relevant products for the purpose of their sale (by the person or another person);


(b)the exposure of relevant products for sale;


(c)the supply of relevant products to retail customers.


(3\)The Welsh Ministers may by regulations create exceptions to the prohibition in [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2).


(4\)The Welsh Ministers must by regulations make provision for and in connection with the grant of personal licences and premises licences.


(5\)Before making regulations under this section the Welsh Ministers must consult any persons that the Welsh Ministers consider it appropriate to consult.


(6\)[Schedule 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3) makes further provision about regulations under [subsection (4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-4).


(7\)Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(8\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes variation or renewal;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>”, in relation to the doing of things or the use of premises in a county or county borough in Wales, means the council of the county or county borough;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” means a licence that is granted by a licensing authority and authorises an individual to do the things mentioned in <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1">subsection (1)</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1-a">(a)</a>, <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1-b">(b)</a> and <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1-c">(c)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” means a licence that is granted by a licensing authority and authorises the use of premises by a person for the things mentioned in <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2">subsection (2)</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2-a">(a)</a>, <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2-b">(b)</a> and <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2-c">(c)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant products</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>tobacco products;
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>herbal smoking products;
</p></div><div><div>(c)</div><p>cigarette papers;
</p></div><div><div>(d)</div><p>vaping products;
</p></div><div><div>(e)</div><p>nicotine products;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>supply</span>” includes despatch.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I25S. 19 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

#### 20Offences in connection with licences: Wales

(1\)A person who breaches the prohibition in [section 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-1) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-2) commits an offence.


(2\)A person commits an offence if—


(a)the person provides information to a licensing authority—


(i)in, or in connection with, an application for the grant of a personal licence or a premises licence, or


(ii)in pursuance of any other obligation imposed by or under regulations made under [section 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19)[(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-4),


(b)the information is false or misleading in a material respect, and


(c)the person knows, or ought reasonably to know, that the information is false or misleading in a material respect.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on summary conviction to a fine.


(4\)The court by which a person is convicted of an offence under [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-20-1) may order the relevant products to which the offence relates, and any container for them, to be forfeited and either destroyed or dealt with in such other manner as the court may order.


(5\)In this section—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes variation or renewal;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>”, in relation to the doing of things or the use of premises in a county or county borough in Wales, means the council of the county or county borough;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant product</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>.
</p></li></ul>

(1\)A local weights and measures authority in Wales may impose a financial penalty on a person if satisfied that—

### Restricted premises orders

Prospective

#### 23Restricted premises orders

(1\)Where a person convicted of a relevant offence is a persistent offender, the person who brought the proceedings for the offence may by complaint to a magistrates’ court apply for a restricted premises order to be made in respect of the premises in relation to which the offence was committed (“the relevant premises”).


(2\)A magistrates’ court may make the restricted premises order only if satisfied that the applicant has complied with [section 24](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24-1) (notice to interested persons).


(3\)A “restricted premises order” is an order prohibiting the sale on the relevant premises of any one or more of the following—


(a)tobacco products;


(b)herbal smoking products;


(c)cigarette papers;


(d)vaping products;


(e)nicotine products.


(4\)The prohibition imposed by a restricted premises order applies to sales whether made by the offender or any other person.


(5\)A restricted premises order has effect for the period specified in the order, which may not exceed one year.


(6\)A restricted premises order is a local land charge and in respect of that charge the applicant for the order is the originating authority for the purposes of the Local Land Charges Act 1975\.


(7\)A person convicted of a relevant offence is a “persistent offender” for the purposes of [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23) if, on at least two other occasions within the period of two years ending with the date of the offence, the person committed a relevant offence in relation to the relevant premises.


(8\)In this section “relevant offence” means—


(a)an offence under any of the following provisions of this Part—


(i)section [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1) (sale of tobacco etc to people born on or after 1 January 2009\);


(ii)section [3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-3) (tobacco vending machines);


(iii)section [10](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10) (sale of vaping or nicotine products to under 18s);


(iv)section [12](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-12) (vaping and nicotine product vending machines);


(b)an offence under any of the following (which are repealed by this Act)—


(i)section 7 of the Children and Young Persons Act 1933 (sale of tobacco, etc., to under 18s);


(ii)section 3A of the Children and Young Persons (Protection from Tobacco) Act 1991 (tobacco vending machines);


(iii)section 92 of the Children and Families Act 2014 (sale of nicotine products to under 18s).


Commencement Information

I29S. 23 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 24Restricted premises orders: interested persons

(1\)An applicant for a restricted premises order must, after making reasonable enquiries, give notice of the application to anyone appearing to the applicant to be an interested person.


(2\)An interested person may make representations to the court as to why the order should not be made.


(3\)If a restricted premises order is made without an interested person having been given a notice under [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24-1), and without them having made representations to the court, the person may by complaint apply to the court for an order varying or discharging the restricted premises order.


(4\)On an application under [subsection (3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24-3) the court may, after hearing the interested person and the applicant for the restricted premises order, make such order varying or discharging the restricted premises order as it considers appropriate.


(5\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24) “interested person”, in relation to an application for a restricted premises order, means—


(a)the occupier of the premises, and


(b)any other person who has an interest in the premises.


Commencement Information

I30S. 24 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 25Restricted premises orders: appeals

An appeal against an order made under [section 23](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23) or [24](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-24) may be brought to the Crown Court.


Commencement Information

I31S. 25 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 26Breach of restricted premises orders

(1\)A person commits an offence if the person—


(a)sells anything in breach of a restricted premises order, and


(b)knows, or ought reasonably to know, that the sale is in breach of the order.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to prove that the person took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23) is liable on summary conviction to a fine.


Commencement Information

I32S. 26 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 27Power to extend restricted premises orders in Wales

(1\)The Welsh Ministers may by regulations amend section [23](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23) so as to add an offence to the definition of “relevant offence” where that offence is committed on premises in Wales.


(2\)Regulations may be made under subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-27-1) only if the additional offence relates to tobacco products, herbal smoking products, cigarette papers, vaping products or nicotine products.


(3\)Before making regulations under this section the Welsh Ministers must consult any persons that they consider it appropriate to consult.


(4\)Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I33S. 27 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I34S. 27 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Restricted sale orders

#### 28Restricted sale orders

(1\)Where a person convicted of a relevant offence is a persistent offender, the person who brought the proceedings for the offence may by complaint to a magistrates’ court apply for a restricted sale order against the offender.


(2\)A “restricted sale order” is an order prohibiting the offender—


(a)from selling any one or more of the following—


(i)tobacco products,


(ii)herbal smoking products,


(iii)cigarette papers,


(iv)vaping products,


(v)nicotine products;


(b)from having any management functions in respect of any premises in so far as those functions relate to the sale of anything listed in [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28-2-a)[(i)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28-2-a-i) to [(v)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28-2-a-v).


(3\)A restricted sale order has effect for the period specified in the order, which may not exceed one year.


(4\)A person convicted of a relevant offence is a “persistent offender” for the purposes of [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28) if, on at least two other occasions within the period of two years ending with the date of the offence, the person committed a relevant offence.


(5\)In this section “relevant offence” means—


(a)an offence under any of the following provisions of this Part—


(i)section [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1) (sale of tobacco etc to people born on or after 1 January 2009\);


(ii)section [3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-3) (tobacco vending machines);


(iii)section [10](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10) (sale of vaping or nicotine products to under 18s);


(iv)section [12](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-12) (vaping and nicotine product vending machines);


(b)an offence under any of the following (which are repealed by this Act)—


(i)section 7 of the Children and Young Persons Act 1933 (sale of tobacco, etc., to under 18s);


(ii)section 3A of the Children and Young Persons (Protection from Tobacco) Act 1991 (tobacco vending machines);


(iii)section 92 of the Children and Families Act 2014 (sale of nicotine products to under 18s).


Commencement Information

I35S. 28 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 29Restricted sale orders: appeals

An appeal against an order made under [section 28](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28) may be brought to the Crown Court.


Commencement Information

I36S. 29 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 30Breach of restricted sale orders

(1\)A person who fails to comply with a restricted sale order commits an offence.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to prove that the person took all reasonable steps to avoid the commission of the offence.


(3\)A person who commits an offence under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-30) is liable on summary conviction to a fine.


Commencement Information

I37S. 30 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Offences by bodies

#### 31Liability of others for certain offences committed by bodies

(1\)Where an offence under [section 26](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-26) is committed by a body and the offence is committed with the consent or connivance of a relevant person in relation to the body, or a person purporting to act in the capacity of a relevant person in relation to the body, the person (as well as the body) commits the offence and is liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.


(2\)Where any other offence under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1), or under any regulations under section [13](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13) or [14](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14)—


(a)is committed with the consent or connivance of a relevant person in relation to the body, or a person purporting to act in the capacity of a relevant person in relation to the body, or


(b)is attributable to neglect on the part of such a person,


the person (as well as the body) commits the offence and is liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.


(3\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-31)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>body</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>a body corporate,
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>a partnership, or
</p></div><div><div>(c)</div><p>an unincorporated association;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>relevant person</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>in relation to a body corporate other than one whose affairs are managed by its members, a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body;
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>in relation to a limited liability partnership or other body corporate whose affairs are managed by its members, a member who exercises functions of management with respect to it;
</p></div><div><div>(c)</div><p>in relation to a limited partnership, a general partner (within the meaning given by section 3 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907);
</p></div><div><div>(d)</div><p>in relation to any other partnership, a partner;
</p></div><div><div>(e)</div><p>in relation to an unincorporated association, a person who exercises functions of management with respect to it.
</p></div></div></div></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I38S. 31 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Enforcement functions

#### 32Enforcement authorities

(1\)It is the duty of each relevant enforcement authority in England and local weights and measures authority in Wales to enforce within its area the provisions of [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) and any regulations under section [13](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13) or [14](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14).


(2\)In this Part “relevant enforcement authority in England” means—


(a)a local weights and measures authority in England, and


(b)in relation to the enforcement of sections 16 to 18 (retail licensing: England), in addition, any district council in England that—


(i)is specified as a licensing authority under paragraph 2 of Schedule 1, and


(ii)is not a local weights and measures authority.


(3\)In Schedule 5 to the Consumer Rights Act 2015 (investigatory powers), in paragraph 10 (enforcer’s legislation), at the appropriate place (according to date of enactment) insert—


<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32"><span>32</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026.<span>”</span></span>
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I39S. 32 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 33Programme of enforcement action: England

(1\)Each relevant enforcement authority in England must, at least once a year, consider—


(a)whether it is appropriate to carry out a programme of enforcement action in its area, and


(b)if so, what that programme should involve.


(2\)In [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-33-1) “programme of enforcement action” means a programme involving one or more of the following—


(a)the investigation of complaints in respect of an alleged offence under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) or any regulations under section [13](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13);


(b)the bringing of prosecutions in respect of such an offence;


(c)the taking of other measures intended to reduce the incidence of such offences.


Commencement Information

I40S. 33 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 34Programme of enforcement action: Wales

(1\)Each local weights and measures authority in Wales must, at least once a year, consider—


(a)whether it is appropriate to carry out a programme of enforcement action in its area, and


(b)if so, what that programme should involve.


(2\)In [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-33-1) “programme of enforcement action” means a programme involving one or more of the following—


(a)the investigation of complaints in respect of an alleged offence that is a listed offence;


(b)the bringing of prosecutions in respect of a listed offence;


(c)the taking of other measures intended to reduce the incidence of listed offences.


(3\)In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34) “listed offence” means—


(a)an offence under any provision of [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) or regulations under [section 14](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14), or


(b)an offence under either of the following provisions of the Public Health (Wales) Act [2017 (anaw 2\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2017/2)—


<ul><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13230">section 51A</a> (offence of handing over tobacco etc. to people born on or after 1 January 2009);
</p></li><li><p>section 52 (offence of handing over vaping or nicotine products to under 18s).
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I41S. 34 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Powers of ministers to take over enforcement

#### 35Power of ministers to take over enforcement functions

(1\)The Secretary of State may direct that, in relation to cases of a particular description or a particular case, the duty imposed by [section 32](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32-1) on a relevant enforcement authority in England is to be discharged by the Secretary of State and not by the authority.


(2\)The Welsh Ministers may direct that, in relation to cases of a particular description or a particular case, the duty imposed by [section 32](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32-1) on a local weights and measures authority in Wales is to be discharged by the Welsh Ministers and not by the authority.


Commencement Information

I42S. 35 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 36Power of ministers to take over proceedings

(1\)The Secretary of State may take over the conduct of any proceedings from a relevant enforcement authority in England in respect of an offence committed under this Part or any regulations under section [13](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13).


(2\)The Welsh Ministers may take over the conduct of any proceedings from a local weights and measures authority in Wales in respect of an offence committed under this Part or any regulations under section [14](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14).


Commencement Information

I43S. 36 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Fixed penalties: England

Prospective

#### 37Fixed penalty notices: England

(1\)A relevant enforcement authority in England that has reason to believe that a person has committed an offence under, or under regulations made under, any of the following may give the person a fixed penalty notice in respect of the offence—


<ul><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1">section 1</a> (sale of tobacco etc to people born on or after 1 January 2009);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2">section 2</a> (purchase of tobacco etc on behalf of others);
</p></li><li><p>section <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5">5</a> (age of sale notice at point of sale: England);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10">section 10</a> (sale of vaping or nicotine products to under 18s);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-11">section 11</a> (purchase of vaping or nicotine products on behalf of under 18s);
</p></li><li><p>section <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-13">13</a> (displays of products or prices in England);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-15">section 15</a> (free distribution and discount of products);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17">section 17</a> (offences in connection with retail licences: England).
</p></li></ul>

(2\)A fixed penalty notice is a notice offering a person the opportunity to discharge any liability to conviction for the offence to which the notice relates by payment of an amount specified in the notice within the relevant period.


(3\)The amount specified in a fixed penalty notice in respect of an offence under [section 17](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17) must be an amount equal to level 4 on the standard scale of fines for summary offences.


(4\)The amount specified in a fixed penalty notice in respect of any other offence must be £200\.


(5\)For the purposes of [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37) “the relevant period” is the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the fixed penalty notice is given.


(6\)A fixed penalty notice must explain—


(a)that the relevant enforcement authority in England has reason to believe that the person has committed the offence, and why,


(b)the effect of [subsection (7\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37-7), and


(c)when and how payment may be made.


(7\)Where a fixed penalty notice has been given to a person (and has not been withdrawn)—


(a)no proceedings may be instituted for the offence before the end of the relevant period, and


(b)the person may not be convicted of the offence if the person pays—


(i)the full amount of the fixed penalty in the notice before the end of the relevant period, or


(ii)50% of that amount before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the relevant period starts.


(8\)Where proceedings are instituted for the offence after the end of the relevant period, that period is to be disregarded for the purposes of calculating the period mentioned in section 127(1\) of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980\.


(9\)A fixed penalty notice given under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37) may be withdrawn by the relevant enforcement authority in England that gave it at any time before a payment is made in pursuance of the notice.


Commencement Information

I44S. 37 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

#### 38Fixed penalties in England: use of proceeds

(1\)Any sums received by a relevant enforcement authority in England in pursuance of a fixed penalty notice must be used in connection with any functions they have under or under regulations made under—


(a)this Act;


(b)Part 1 of the Health Act 2006;


(c)the Tobacco and Related Products Regulations 2016 ([S.I. 2016/507](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/uksi/2016/507)).


(2\)In this section “fixed penalty notice” means a fixed penalty notice given under [section 37](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37).


Commencement Information

I45S. 38 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 39Power to change amount of fixed penalties: England

(1\)The Secretary of State may by regulations amend [section 37](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37) in relation to the giving of fixed penalty notices in respect of any offence other than an offence under [section 17](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17) so as to—


(a)change the amount which must be specified in notices, or


(b)change the percentage discount for early payment.


(2\)The amount mentioned in subsection [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-39-1)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-39-1-a) must not be changed to an amount that exceeds level 3 on the standard scale of fines for summary offences.


(3\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-39) are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I46S. 39 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I47S. 39 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 40Fixed penalty notices: Wales

(1\)A local weights and measures authority in Wales that has reason to believe that a person has committed an offence under, or under regulations made under, any of the following may give the person a fixed penalty notice in respect of the offence—


<ul><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1">section 1</a> (sale of tobacco etc to people born on or after 1 January 2009);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2">section 2</a> (purchase of tobacco etc on behalf of others);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-6">section 6</a> (age of sale notice at point of sale: Wales);
</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-10">section 10</a> (sale of vaping or nicotine products to under 18s);

</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-14">section 14</a> (displays of products or prices in Wales);

</p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-20">section 20</a> (offences in connection with retail licences: Wales).
</p></li></ul>

(2\)A fixed penalty notice is a notice offering a person the opportunity to discharge any liability to conviction for the offence to which the notice relates by payment of an amount specified in the notice within the relevant period.


(3\)The amount specified in a fixed penalty notice in respect of an offence under [section 20](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-20) must be an amount equal to level 4 on the standard scale of fines for summary offences.


(4\)The amount specified in a fixed penalty notice in respect of any other offence must be £200\.


(5\)For the purposes of this section “the relevant period” is the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the fixed penalty notice is given.


(6\)A fixed penalty notice must explain—


(a)that the local weights and measures authority has reason to believe that the person has committed the offence, and why,


(b)the effect of [subsection (7\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40-7), and


(c)when and how payment may be made.


(7\)Where a fixed penalty notice has been given to a person (and has not been withdrawn)—


(a)no proceedings may be instituted for the offence before the end of the relevant period, and


(b)the person may not be convicted of the offence if the person pays—


(i)the full amount of the fixed penalty in the notice before the end of the relevant period, or


(ii)50% of that amount before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the relevant period starts.


(8\)Where proceedings are instituted for the offence after the end of the relevant period, that period is to be disregarded for the purposes of calculating the period mentioned in section 127(1\) of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980\.


(9\)A fixed penalty notice given under this section may be withdrawn by the local weights and measures authority that gave it at any time before a payment is made in pursuance of the notice.

#### 47Transitional provision: general

(1\)In relation to times before 1 January 2027—


(a)[sections 23](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23)[(8\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-23-8), [28](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28)[(5\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-28-5), [37](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37-1) and [40](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40-1) have effect as if they did not include a reference to section [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1), [2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2), [5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) or [6](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-6);


(b)a reference in [section 31](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-31)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-31-2), [32](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32-1), [33](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-33)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-33-2), [34](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34)[(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34-3) or [36](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-36)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-36-1) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-36-2) to “[this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1)” does not include a reference to section [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1), [2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2), [5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5) or [6](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-6).


(2\)In relation to times before [section 17](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17) comes into force, [section 37](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37-1) and [(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-37-3) have effect as if those provisions did not include a reference to that section.


(3\)In relation to times before [section 20](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-20) comes into force, [section 40](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40)[(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40-1) and [(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-40-3) have effect as if those provisions did not include a reference to that section.


(4\)In relation to times before section [51A](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13326) of the Public Health (Wales) Act [2017 (anaw 2\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2017/2) comes into force, section [34](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34)[(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34-3) has effect as if it did not include a reference to that section.


(5\)In relation to times before section 52 of the Public Health (Wales) Act [2017 (anaw 2\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2017/2) comes into force, section [34](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34)[(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-34-3) has effect as if it did not include a reference to that section.


(6\)In relation to times before the repeal by this Act of the Tobacco Advertising and Promotion Act 2002 comes fully into force (see Schedule [21](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-21) to this Act), sections [38](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-38) and [41](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-41) have effect as if they each included a reference to that Act.


Commencement Information

I57S. 47 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Powers to adjust scope

#### 48Power to extend Part 1 to other products

(1\)The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this Part for the purpose of extending any provision that applies in relation to a tobacco product to—


(a)a filter that does not form part of a tobacco product or herbal smoking product;


(b)a tobacco related device.


(2\)The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this Part for the purpose of extending to filters any provision made by sections [7](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-7) to [9](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-9) in relation to a relevant oral tobacco product.


(3\)Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must consult any persons the Secretary of State considers it appropriate to consult.


(4\)Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers if the regulations contain provision which would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if contained in an Act of the Senedd.


(5\)Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I58S. 48 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I59S. 48 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Crown application

#### 49Crown application

(1\)[This Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) and regulations made under it bind the Crown.


(2\)Nothing in [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) or regulations made under it makes the Crown criminally liable.


(3\)The High Court may declare unlawful any act or omission for which the Crown would be criminally liable if it were not for [subsection (2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-49-2).


(4\)[Subsection (2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-49-2) does not affect the criminal liability of persons in the service of the Crown.


Commencement Information

I60S. 49 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2)

I61S. 49 in force at 29\.9\.2026 in so far as not already in force, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Prospective

### Interpretation etc

#### 50Interpretation of Part 1

In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>cigarette papers</span>” includes anything intended to be used for encasing tobacco products or herbal smoking products for the purpose of enabling them to be smoked;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>filter</span>” means a filter that is intended to be used when smoking a tobacco product or herbal smoking product (including a filter that forms part of, or that is intended to be inserted into, an item such as a cigarette holder or pipe);
</p></li><li><p>“<span>herbal smoking product</span>” means a product consisting wholly or partly of vegetable matter and intended to be smoked but not containing tobacco;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>medical device</span>” has the meaning given by the Medical Devices Regulations 2002 (<a href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/uksi/2002/618">S.I. 2002/618</a>);
</p></li><li><p>“<span>medicinal product</span>” has the meaning given by the Human Medicines Regulations 2012 (<a href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/uksi/2012/1916">S.I. 2012/1916</a>);
</p></li><li><p>“<span>nicotine product</span>” has the meaning given by section <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-51">51</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises</span>” means any place (including a vehicle or moveable structure);
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant enforcement authority in England</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32">section 32</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-32-2">(2)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>retail packaging</span>”, in relation to a product, means the packaging in which it is, or is intended to be, presented for sale by retail;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>sell</span>” means sell by retail;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>tobacco product</span>” means a product consisting wholly or partly of tobacco and intended to be smoked, sniffed, sucked, chewed or consumed in any other way;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>tobacco related device</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>a device, other than a vape, which enables a tobacco product to be consumed (for example, a heated tobacco device or pipe), or
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>an item which is intended to form part of such a device;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>tobacco retailer</span>” means a person who carries on a business involving the sale of tobacco products by retail;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>vape</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>a device which—
</p><div><div><div><div>(i)</div><p>vaporises substances, other than tobacco, for the purpose of inhalation through a mouthpiece (whether or not it also vaporises tobacco), and
</p></div><div><div>(ii)</div><p>is not a medical device or a medicinal product, or
</p></div></div></div></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>an item which is intended to form part of a device within paragraph (a) (including anything intended to be attached to it with a view to imparting flavour);
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>vaping product</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>a vape, or
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>a vaping substance;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>vaping substance</span>” means a substance, other than tobacco, that is intended to be vaporised by a vape;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>vaporises</span>” includes aerosolises (and “<span>vaporised</span>” is to be construed accordingly);
</p></li><li><p>“<span>vehicle</span>” means every type of vehicle, including a vessel, aircraft and hovercraft.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I62S. 50 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

#### 51Meaning of “nicotine product”

(1\)In this Part “nicotine product” means—


(a)a device which is intended to enable nicotine to be delivered into the human body,


(b)an item which is intended to form part of a device within paragraph [(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-51-1-a),


(c)nicotine, or any substance containing nicotine, which is intended to be delivered into the human body, or


(d)an item containing anything within paragraph [(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-51-1-c).


(2\)But the following are not “nicotine products” for the purposes of this section—


(a)a tobacco product;


(b)a herbal smoking product;


(c)cigarette papers;


(d)any device which is intended to be used for the consumption of tobacco products or herbal smoking products;


(e)a vaping product;


(f)a medical device;


(g)a medicinal product.


Commencement Information

I63S. 51 in force at 29\.9\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)
