(2\)A person who has management responsibilities for a heated tobacco\-free vehicle must make sure that signs are displayed in that vehicle in accordance with any requirements imposed by regulations.


(3\)The signs must indicate that the use of heated tobacco devices is prohibited in the place or vehicle.


(4\)Regulations under paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11489) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11493) may, in particular, impose requirements about—

(b)how and where signs are to be displayed.

(6\)A person who fails to comply with the duty in paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11489) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11493) commits an offence.

(9\)A person guilty of an offence under paragraph [(6\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11520) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.


###### Offences relating to use of heated tobacco devices

###### 9GOffence of using heated tobacco device

(1\)A person who uses a heated tobacco device in a heated tobacco\-free place or vehicle commits an offence.


(2\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11559) to show that they did not know, and could not reasonably have been expected to know, that it was a heated tobacco\-free place or vehicle.


(3\)If a person charged with an offence under this Article relies on the defence in paragraph [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11563), and evidence is adduced which is sufficient to raise an issue with respect to that defence, the court must assume that the defence is satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is not.


(4\)A person guilty of an offence under this Article is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.


###### 9HOffence of failing to prevent use of heated tobacco device

(1\)A person who controls or is concerned in the management of a heated tobacco\-free place must cause a person using a heated tobacco device there to stop using the device.


(2\)The driver of a heated tobacco\-free vehicle, and any other person specified in regulations, must cause a person using a heated tobacco device in the vehicle to stop using the device.


(3\)A person who fails to comply with the duty in paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11580) or [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11584) commits an offence.


(4\)It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under paragraph [(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11588) to show—


(a)that they took reasonable steps to cause the person in question to stop using the heated tobacco device,


(b)that they did not know, and could not reasonably have been expected to know, that the person in question was using a heated tobacco device, or


(c)that on other grounds it was reasonable for them not to comply with the duty.


(5\)If a person charged with an offence under paragraph [(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11588) relies on a defence in paragraph [(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11594), and evidence is adduced which is sufficient to raise an issue with respect to that defence, the court must assume that the defence is satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is not.


(6\)A person guilty of an offence under paragraph [(3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11588) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.”


(4\)In Article 15 (regulations), in paragraph (3\)(a), after “, [9A](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11170)” (inserted by section [161](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-161) of this Act) insert “, [9E](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p11438)”.

### Ships

#### 164Power to prohibit vaping etc on ships

(1\)Section 85 of the Merchant Shipping Act 1995 (safety and health on ships) is amended as follows.


(2\)In subsection (8\)—


(a)in the words before paragraph (a)—


(i)after “prohibition of smoking” insert “or the use of relevant vapes or heated tobacco devices”;


(ii)for “smoking provisions” substitute “relevant provisions”;


(b)in paragraph (a), for “smoking provisions” substitute “relevant provisions”;


(c)in paragraph (b), at the end insert “in relation to the relevant provisions”;


(d)in paragraph (c)—


(i)after “enforcement functions” insert “in relation to the relevant provisions”;


(ii)after “authorised officers have” insert “in relation to smoking”;


(iii)for “(which confers powers of entry, etc., on authorised officers of enforcement authorities in relation to the enforcement of the provisions of that Act in relation to smoking)” substitute “(powers of entry)”;


(e)for paragraph (d) substitute—


“(d)in relation to an offence of smoking or using a relevant vape or heated tobacco device in a place where to do so is prohibited under the relevant provisions, for purposes corresponding to those of section 9 and Schedule 1 to the Health Act 2006 (fixed penalties).”;


(f)omit the words after paragraph (d).


(3\)After subsection (8\) insert—


“(9\)In subsection (8\)—


<ul><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>heated tobacco device</span></span><span>” means a device that heats tobacco to generate a vapour or an aerosol for the purpose of inhalation through a mouthpiece (whether or not it can also heat other matter to produce a vapour or aerosol);</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>relevant vape</span></span><span>” means a vape that is not a heated tobacco device;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>smoking</span></span><span>” has the same meaning as in Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the Health Act 2006;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>vape</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-50"><span>50</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026.<span>”</span></span>
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I185S. 164 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(3\)(a)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/3/a)

Part 8General
-------------

### 165Review of Act

(1\)The Secretary of State must—


(a)carry out a review of the operation of this Act during the relevant period, and


(b)prepare and lay before Parliament a report setting out the conclusions of that review.


(2\)In carrying out the review the Secretary of State must, in particular—


(a)consider any evidence as to the economic or health impacts of the Act, and


(b)consult—


(i)the Welsh Ministers,


(ii)the Scottish Ministers, and


(iii)the Department of Health in Northern Ireland.


(3\)In this section “the relevant period” means such period as the Secretary of State considers appropriate being a period of not less than 4 years, nor more than 7 years, beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.


Commencement Information

I186S. 165 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 166Application to Parliament

To the extent that this Act or regulations made under it would not (but for this section) apply in relation to the Parliamentary Estate, they do so apply.


Commencement Information

I187S. 166 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 167Further consequential amendments

I188S. 167 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 168Power of Secretary of State to make consequential provision

(1\)The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential on this Act.


(2\)Regulations under this section may amend, repeal or revoke legislation passed or made before, or in the same Session as, this Act (including provision made by this Act).


(3\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-168) that amend, repeal or revoke primary legislation are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(4\)Any other regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-168) are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


(5\)In this section “primary legislation” means—


(a)an Act of Parliament,


(b)an Act of the Scottish Parliament,


(c)an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru, or


(d)Northern Ireland legislation.


Commencement Information

I189S. 168 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 169Power of Scottish Ministers to make consequential provision

(1\)The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make provision that is consequential on any of the following—


(a)[Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-2) (sale and distribution);


(b)[sections 148](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-148) to [152](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-152) and [Schedule 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-18) (smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and other free\-from places: Scotland).


(2\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-169) may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by or under—


(a)an Act passed—


(i)before this Act, or


(ii)later in the same session of Parliament as this Act, or


(b)an Act of the Scottish Parliament passed before this Act.


(3\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-168) that amend or repeal provision made by an Act of the Scottish Parliament, or an Act, are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(4\)Any other regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-168) are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

I190S. 169 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 170Power of Welsh Ministers to make consequential provision

(1\)The Welsh Ministers may by regulations make provision that is consequential on any of the following—


(a)[Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) (sale and distribution);


(b)[sections 153](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-153) to [158](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-158) and [Schedule 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-19) (smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and other free\-from places: Wales).


(2\)The only provision that may be made by virtue of this section is provision that would be within the legislative competence of Senedd Cymru if contained in an Act of the Senedd.


(3\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-169) may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by or under—


(a)an Act passed—


(i)before this Act, or


(ii)later in the same session of Parliament as this Act, or


(b)an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru passed before this Act.


(4\)Regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-170) that amend or repeal provision made by an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru, or an Act, are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(5\)Any other regulations under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-168) are subject to the negative resolution procedure.

### 171Power of Northern Ireland department to make consequential provision

(1\)A Northern Ireland department may by regulations make provision that is consequential on any of the following—


(a)[Part 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-3) (sale and distribution);

(2\)Regulations under this section may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by or under—


(a)an Act passed—


(i)before this Act, or


(ii)later in the same session of Parliament as this Act, or


(b)Northern Ireland legislation passed or made before this Act.


(3\)Regulations under this section that amend, repeal or revoke any provision of an Act or Northern Ireland legislation are subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(4\)Any other regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution procedure.


Commencement Information

### 172Regulations: general

(1\)A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to make—


(a)consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;


(b)different provision for different purposes;


(c)different provision for different parts of the United Kingdom.


(2\)[This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-172) does not apply to regulations under [section 175](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-175), [176](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-176) or [177](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-177).


Commencement Information

I193S. 172 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 173Regulations and orders: procedure

(1\)Regulations made by the Secretary of State under this Act are to be made by statutory instrument.


(2\)For regulations made under this Act by the Scottish Ministers, see section 27 of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act [2010 (asp 10\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/asp/2010/10) (definition of “Scottish statutory instrument”).


(3\)Regulations or orders made by the Welsh Ministers under this Act are to be made by Welsh statutory instrument.


(4\)Any power of a Northern Ireland department to make regulations or orders under this Act is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of the Statutory Rules (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ([S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/nisi/1979/1573)).


(5\)Where regulations under this Act are “subject to the affirmative resolution procedure”, the regulations—


(a)if made by the Secretary of State, may not be made unless a draft of the statutory instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each House of Parliament;


(b)if made by the Welsh Ministers, are subject to the Senedd approval procedure (see Part 2A of the Legislation (Wales) Act [2019 (anaw 4\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2019/4));


(c)if made by the Scottish Ministers, are subject to the affirmative procedure (see section 29 of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act [2010 (asp 10\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/asp/2010/10));


(d)if made by a Northern Ireland department, may not be made unless a draft of the regulations has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, the Northern Ireland Assembly.


(6\)Where regulations under this Act are “subject to the negative resolution procedure”—


(a)if made by the Secretary of State, the statutory instrument containing them is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament;


(b)if made by the Welsh Ministers, the regulations are subject to the Senedd annulment procedure (see Part 2A of the Legislation (Wales) Act [2019 (anaw 4\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2019/4));


(c)if made by the Scottish Ministers, the regulations are subject to the negative procedure (see section 28 of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act [2010 (asp 10\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/asp/2010/10));


(d)if made by a Northern Ireland department, the regulations are subject to negative resolution within the meaning of section 41(6\) of the Interpretation Act (Northern Ireland) [1954 (c. 33 (N.I.))](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/apni/1954/33) as if they were a statutory instrument within the meaning of that Act.


(7\)Any provision that may be made by the Secretary of State or a Northern Ireland department in regulations under this Act subject to the negative resolution procedure may be made by them in regulations subject to the affirmative resolution procedure.


(8\)See also—


(a)section 33 of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act [2010 (asp 10\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/asp/2010/10) (combining Scottish subordinate legislation subject to different procedures);


(b)section 37G of the Legislation (Wales) Act [2019 (anaw 4\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/anaw/2019/4) (combining Welsh subordinate legislation subject to different procedures).


Commencement Information

I194S. 173 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 174Extent

(1\)An amendment or repeal made by this Act has the same extent as the provision amended or repealed.


(2\)Subject to that—


(a)[Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) extends to England and Wales only;


(b)[Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-2) extends to Scotland only;


(c)[Part 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-3) extends to Northern Ireland only;


(d)[Parts 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-4), [5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-5) and [6](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-6) and [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-8) extend to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland.


Commencement Information

I195S. 174 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

(2\)Any provision of, or amendment made by, Parts [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-1) to [3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-3) so far as it confers a power to make regulations or relates to the exercise of the power, comes into force on the day on which this Act is passed.


(3\)The following (which relate to the age of sale of tobacco etc) come into force on 1 January 2027 (so far as not in force by virtue of subsection [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-175-2))—


(a)sections [1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-1), [2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-2), [5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-5), [6](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-6) and [44](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-44)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-44-2) and [Schedule 7](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-7);

(a)[sections 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19) to [22](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-22) and Schedules [3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3) and [4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4) (licensing of retail sales of tobacco products etc in Wales);

(b)[section 43](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-43) and [Schedule 5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-5) (handing over tobacco etc to underage people);


(c)[sections 153](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-153) to [158](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-158) and [Schedule 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-19) (smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and other free\-from places: Wales).


(2\)The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make transitional or saving provision in connection with the coming into force of—


(a)[Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-2) (sale and distribution: Scotland);


(b)[sections 148](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-148) to [152](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-152) and [Schedule 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-18) (smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and other free\-from places: Scotland).


(3\)The Department of Health in Northern Ireland may by regulations make transitional or saving provision in connection with the coming into force of—


(a)[Part 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#part-3) (sale and distribution: Northern Ireland);


(b)[sections 159](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-159) to [163](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-163) and [Schedule 20](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-20) (smoke\-free places, vape\-free places and other free\-from places: Northern Ireland).


(4\)The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving provision in connection with the coming into force of any provision of this Act.


(5\)Transitional provision and savings made under this section are additional, and without prejudice, to those made by or under any other provision of this Act.


(6\)A power conferred by [subsections (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-177-1) to [(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-177-4) includes power to make different provision for different purposes.


(7\)A requirement imposed under or by virtue of this Act to consult any persons may be satisfied by consultation carried out before this Act comes into force.


Commencement Information

I198S. 177 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

### 178Short title

This Act may be cited as the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026\.


Commencement Information

I199S. 178 in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 176(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/176/4)

Schedules
=========

Section 16(6\)

Schedule 1Retail licensing scheme: England
------------------------------------------

### Introduction

1[This Schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1) is about the provision that may be made by regulations under [section 16](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16)[(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-4).


Commencement Information

I200Sch. 1 para. 1 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Licensing authority

2The regulations must specify a description of local authority (a “licensing authority”) which is to grant licences.


Commencement Information

I201Sch. 1 para. 2 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Grant of licence

3(1\)The regulations may—


(a)prohibit a licensing authority from granting a licence unless satisfied as to a matter specified in the regulations;


(b)require a licensing authority to have regard, in deciding whether to grant a licence, to a matter specified in the regulations.


(2\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-3-1)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-3-1-a) includes—


(a)provision prohibiting a licensing authority from granting a premises licence in respect of premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations;


(b)provision limiting the number of licensed premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may make provision requiring a licensing authority not to grant a premises licence unless the premises have been inspected in accordance with the regulations.


Commencement Information

I202Sch. 1 para. 3 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Licence fee

4(1\)The regulations may authorise a licensing authority to charge a fee in respect of an application for the grant of a licence (which may be set at a level that takes into account the cost of exercising functions under or in connection with [sections 16](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16) to [18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18) or the regulations).


(2\)Any such fee must not exceed an amount specified in, or determined in accordance with, the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may require a licensing authority to pay a proportion of any amount received by virtue of [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-4-1) to any other person with functions under or in connection with [sections 16](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16) to [18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18) or the regulations.


Commencement Information

I203Sch. 1 para. 4 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Licence conditions

5(1\)The regulations may make provision for the grant of a licence subject to conditions.


(2\)Provision of the kind mentioned in [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-5-1) may—


(a)enable a licensing authority to attach conditions to a licence;


(b)require a licensing authority to attach to a licence a condition specified in the regulations.


(3\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-5-1) includes provision prohibiting or restricting the sale of relevant products within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


Commencement Information

I204Sch. 1 para. 5 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Duration etc of licence

6(1\)The regulations may make provision about the duration, renewal, variation, suspension or revocation of licences.


(2\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-6-1) includes provision conferring power on a court by which a person is convicted of an offence under [section 17](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-17) to vary, suspend or revoke a licence.


Commencement Information

I205Sch. 1 para. 6 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Publication of licence information

7The regulations may make provision for the publication by a licensing authority of information relating to licences granted by the licensing authority.


Commencement Information

I206Sch. 1 para. 7 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Reviews and appeals

8(1\)The regulations must specify the circumstances in which a person may request a review of a decision taken under the regulations.


(2\)The regulations must confer a right of appeal to the magistrates’ court against a decision taken on a review.


(3\)The regulations may contain provision about time limits for requesting reviews or initiating appeals.


Commencement Information

I207Sch. 1 para. 8 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Guidance

9The regulations may require a licensing authority, in carrying out functions under the regulations, to have regard to guidance published by the Secretary of State.


Commencement Information

I208Sch. 1 para. 9 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Sub\-delegation

10The regulations may confer discretions.


Commencement Information

I209Sch. 1 para. 10 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

### Interpretation

11In [this Schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes vary or renew;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licence</span>” means a personal licence or a premises licence;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1-paragraph-2">paragraph 2</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>local authority</span>” means—
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p>a county council in England;
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p>a district council in England;
</p></div><div><div>(c)</div><p>a London borough council;
</p></div><div><div>(d)</div><p>the Common Council of the City of London (in its capacity as a local authority), the Sub-Treasurer of the Inner Temple or the Under Treasurer of the Middle Temple;
</p></div><div><div>(e)</div><p>the Council of the Isles of Scilly;
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant products</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16">section 16</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-16-8">(8)</a>.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I210Sch. 1 para. 11 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/4)

Prospective

Section 18

Schedule 2Financial penalties for breach of retail licence conditions: England
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Introduction

1(1\)[This Schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2) makes further provision in connection with the imposition of financial penalties under [section 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18).


(2\)In this Schedule “relevant district council” has the meaning given by [section 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18)[(6\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18-6).


Commencement Information

I211Sch. 2 para. 1 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Notices of intent

2(1\)A local weights and measures authority or relevant district council must, before imposing a financial penalty on a person, give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the proposed financial penalty.


(2\)A notice of intent must specify—


(a)the amount of the proposed financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for proposing to impose the penalty,


(c)information about the right to make representations under [paragraph 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-3), and


(d)the date by which any representations must be made.


(3\)The date specified under [sub\-paragraph (2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2-2)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2-2-d) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the notice of intent is given to the person.


(4\)The local weights and measures authority or relevant district council may at any time withdraw the notice of intent, or amend it to reduce the amount of the proposed financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


Commencement Information

I212Sch. 2 para. 2 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Right to make representations

3(1\)A person who is given a notice of intent under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2) may make written representations to the local weights and measures authority or relevant district council that issued the notice about the proposal to impose a financial penalty.


(2\)Any representations must be made within the period (“the period for representations”) ending with the date specified under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2-2)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-2-2-d).


Commencement Information

I213Sch. 2 para. 3 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Final notices

4(1\)After the end of the period for representations the local weights and measures authority or relevant district council must decide whether to impose a financial penalty on the person.


(2\)If the local weights and measures authority or relevant district council decides to impose a financial penalty on the person, the authority or council must give the person written notice (a “final notice”) imposing the penalty.


(3\)A final notice must specify—


(a)the amount of the financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for imposing the penalty,


(c)the date by which the penalty must be paid,


(d)information about the right of appeal under [paragraph 5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-5), and


(e)the consequences of failure to comply with the final notice.


(4\)The date specified under [sub\-paragraph (3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-4-3)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-4-3-c) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the final notice is given to the person.


(5\)The local weights and measures authority or relevant district council may at any time withdraw a final notice, or amend it to reduce the amount of the financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


(6\)A final notice may not be given more than 28 days after the last day of the period for representations.


Commencement Information

I214Sch. 2 para. 4 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Appeals

5(1\)A person on whom a financial penalty is imposed under [section 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-18) may appeal to the magistrates’ court against—


(a)the decision to impose the penalty, or


(b)the amount of the penalty.


(2\)An appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-5) must be brought before the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the day after the day on which the final notice is given to the person in accordance with [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-4).


(3\)On an appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-5) the magistrates’ court may confirm, reduce or cancel the penalty.


(4\)If a person appeals under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-5), the final notice is suspended until the appeal is finally determined, withdrawn or abandoned.


Commencement Information

I215Sch. 2 para. 5 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Recovery

6(1\)[This paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-6) applies if a person fails to pay the whole or part of a financial penalty before the end of the period within which the person is required to pay the penalty.


(2\)The local weights and measures authority or relevant district council that imposed the financial penalty may recover the unpaid amount of the penalty as if it were payable under an order of the county court.


Commencement Information

I216Sch. 2 para. 6 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

### Use of proceeds

7(1\)Any sums received in pursuance of final notices given under [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2-paragraph-4) must be paid into the Consolidated Fund.


(2\)But before paying such sums into the Consolidated Fund the local weights and measures authority or relevant district council may deduct—


(a)the costs of investigating the matters to which the final notices relate, and


(b)the costs of issuing the notices.


Commencement Information

I217Sch. 2 para. 7 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(4\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/4)

Section 19(6\)

Schedule 3Retail licensing scheme: Wales
----------------------------------------

### Introduction

1This Schedule is about the provision that may be made by regulations under [section 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19)[(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-4).


Commencement Information

I218Sch. 3 para. 1 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Grant of licence

2(1\)The regulations may—


(a)prohibit a licensing authority from granting a licence unless satisfied as to a matter specified in the regulations;


(b)require a licensing authority to have regard, in deciding whether to grant a licence, to a matter specified in the regulations.


(2\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-2-1)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-2-1-a) includes—


(a)provision prohibiting a licensing authority from granting a premises licence in respect of premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations;


(b)provision limiting the number of licensed premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may make provision requiring a licensing authority not to grant a premises licence unless the premises have been inspected in accordance with the regulations.


Commencement Information

I219Sch. 3 para. 2 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Licence fee

3(1\)The regulations may authorise a licensing authority to charge a fee in respect of an application for the grant of a licence (which may be set at a level that takes into account the cost of exercising functions under or in connection with [sections 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19) to [21](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-21) or the regulations).


(2\)Any such fee must not exceed an amount specified in, or determined in accordance with, the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may require a licensing authority to pay a proportion of any amount received by virtue of [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-3-1) to any other person with functions under [sections 19](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19) to [21](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-21) or the regulations.


Commencement Information

I220Sch. 3 para. 3 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Licence conditions

4(1\)The regulations may make provision for the grant of a licence subject to conditions.


(2\)Provision of the kind mentioned in [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-4-1) may—


(a)enable a licensing authority to attach conditions to a licence;


(b)require a licensing authority to attach to a licence a condition specified in the regulations.


(3\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-4-1) includes provision prohibiting or restricting the sale of relevant products within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


Commencement Information

I221Sch. 3 para. 4 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Duration etc of licence

5(1\)The regulations may make provision about the duration, renewal, variation, suspension or revocation of licences.


(2\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-3-paragraph-5-1) includes provision conferring power on a court by which a person is convicted of an offence under [section 20](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-20) to vary, suspend or revoke a licence.


Commencement Information

I222Sch. 3 para. 5 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Publication of licence information

6The regulations may make provision for the publication by a licensing authority of information relating to licences granted by the licensing authority.


Commencement Information

I223Sch. 3 para. 6 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Reviews and appeals

7(1\)The regulations must specify the circumstances in which a person may request a review of a decision taken under the regulations.


(2\)The regulations must confer a right of appeal to the magistrates’ court against a decision taken on a review.


(3\)The regulations may contain provision about time limits for requesting reviews or initiating appeals.


Commencement Information

I224Sch. 3 para. 7 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Guidance

8The regulations may require a licensing authority, in carrying out functions under the regulations, to have regard to guidance published by the Welsh Ministers.


Commencement Information

I225Sch. 3 para. 8 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Sub\-delegation

9The regulations may confer discretions.


Commencement Information

I226Sch. 3 para. 9 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

### Interpretation

10In [this Schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-1)—


<ul><li><p>“<span>grant</span>” includes vary or renew;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licence</span>” means a personal licence or a premises licence;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>licensing authority</span>”, in relation to the doing of things or the use of premises in a county or county borough in Wales, means the council of the county or county borough;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>personal licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>premises licence</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>;
</p></li><li><p>“<span>relevant products</span>” has the meaning given by <a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19">section 19</a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-19-8">(8)</a>.
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I227Sch. 3 para. 10 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/5)

Prospective

Section 21

Schedule 4Financial penalties for breach of retail licence conditions: Wales
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Introduction

1[This Schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-2) makes further provision in connection with the imposition of financial penalties under [section 21](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-21).


Commencement Information

I228Sch. 4 para. 1 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Notices of intent

2(1\)A local weights and measures authority must, before imposing a financial penalty on a person, give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the proposed financial penalty.


(2\)A notice of intent must specify—


(a)the amount of the proposed financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for proposing to impose the penalty,


(c)information about the right to make representations under [paragraph 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-3), and


(d)the date by which any representations must be made.


(3\)The date specified under [sub\-paragraph (2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2-2)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2-2-d) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the notice of intent is given to the person.


(4\)The local weights and measures authority may at any time withdraw the notice of intent, or amend it to reduce the amount of the proposed financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


Commencement Information

I229Sch. 4 para. 2 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Right to make representations

3(1\)A person who is given a notice of intent under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2) may make written representations to the local weights and measures authority that issued the notice about the proposal to impose a financial penalty.


(2\)Any representations must be made within the period (“the period for representations”) ending with the date specified under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2-2)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-2-2-d).


Commencement Information

I230Sch. 4 para. 3 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Final notices

4(1\)After the end of the period for representations the local weights and measures authority must decide whether to impose a financial penalty on the person.


(2\)If the local weights and measures authority decides to impose a financial penalty on the person, the authority must give the person written notice (a “final notice”) imposing the penalty.


(3\)A final notice must specify—


(a)the amount of the financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for imposing the penalty,


(c)the date by which the penalty must be paid,


(d)information about the right of appeal under [paragraph 5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-5), and


(e)the consequences of failure to comply with the final notice.


(4\)The date specified under [sub\-paragraph (3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-4-3)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-4-3-c) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the final notice is given to the person.


(5\)The local weights and measures authority may at any time withdraw a final notice, or amend it to reduce the amount of the financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


(6\)A final notice may not be given more than 28 days after the last day of the period for representations.


Commencement Information

I231Sch. 4 para. 4 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Appeals

5(1\)A person on whom a financial penalty is imposed under [section 21](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-21) may appeal to the magistrates’ court against—


(a)the decision to impose the penalty, or


(b)the amount of the penalty.


(2\)An appeal under this paragraph must be brought before the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the day after the day on which the final notice is given to the person in accordance with [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-4).


(3\)On an appeal under this paragraph the magistrates’ court may confirm, reduce or cancel the penalty.


(4\)If a person appeals under this paragraph, the final notice is suspended until the appeal is finally determined, withdrawn or abandoned.


Commencement Information

I232Sch. 4 para. 5 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Recovery

6(1\)This paragraph applies if a person fails to pay the whole or part of a financial penalty before the end of the period within which the person is required to pay the penalty.


(2\)The local weights and measures authority that imposed the financial penalty may recover the unpaid amount of the penalty as if it were payable under an order of the county court.


Commencement Information

I233Sch. 4 para. 6 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### Use of proceeds

7(1\)Any sums received in pursuance of final notices given under [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-4-paragraph-4) must be paid into the Welsh Consolidated Fund.


(2\)But before paying such sums into the Welsh Consolidated Fund the local weights and measures authority may deduct—


(a)the costs of investigating the matters to which the final notices relate, and


(b)the costs of issuing the notices.


Commencement Information

I234Sch. 4 para. 7 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### “51AY drosedd o roi tybaco etc. i bobl a anwyd ar neu ar ôl 1 Ionawr 2009

(1\)Mae person (“A”) yn cyflawni trosedd—


(a)os yw A, mewn cysylltiad â threfniadau o dan adran 53, yn rhoi yng Nghymru gynhyrchion tybaco, cynhyrchion smygu llysieuol neu bapurau sigaréts i berson a anwyd ar neu ar ôl 1 Ionawr 2009 (“B”),


(b)os nad yw’r rhoi yn digwydd naill ai—


(i)yng nghwrs crefft, proffesiwn, busnes neu gyflogaeth B, neu


(ii)yng ngŵydd person arall a anwyd cyn 1 Ionawr 2009,


(c)os yw A, ar adeg y rhoi, yn gwybod bod cynhyrchion tybaco, cynhyrchion smygu llysieuol neu bapurau sigaréts (pa un bynnag sy’n gymwys) yn cael eu rhoi, a


(d)pan roddir y cynhyrchion tybaco, y cynhyrchion smygu llysieuol neu’r papurau sigaréts, os nad ydynt mewn pecyn—


(i)sydd wedi ei selio, a


(ii)sydd â chyfeiriad arno, at ddiben ei ddanfon i’r cyfeiriad hwnnw yn unol â threfniadau o fewn adran 53\.


(2\)Ystyr “pecyn” yn isadran [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13232)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13255) yw pecyn yn ychwanegol at y pecyn gwreiddiol y mae’r cynhyrchion tybaco, y cynhyrchion smygu llysieuol neu’r papurau sigaréts wedi eu cyflenwi ynddo at ddiben eu gwerthu drwy fanwerthu gan eu gwneuthurwr neu eu mewnforiwr.


(3\)Mae person sy’n euog o drosedd o dan yr adran hon yn agored ar euogfarn ddiannod i ddirwy nad yw’n uwch na lefel 4 ar y raddfa safonol.


(4\)Pan fo person (“y cyhuddedig”) wedi ei gyhuddo o drosedd o dan yr adran hon oherwydd ymddygiad y cyhuddedig ei hun (ac eithrio yn rhinwedd adran 44 o Ddeddf Llysoedd Ynadon [1980 (p.43\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/1980/43) (helpwyr ac anogwyr)) mae’n amddiffyniad i’r cyhuddedig ddangos—


(a)bod y cyhuddedig yn credu, pan ddigwyddodd y rhoi, fod y person y rhoddwyd y cynhyrchion tybaco, y cynhyrchion smygu llysieuol neu’r papurau sigaréts iddo, neu berson arall a oedd yn bresennol ar adeg y rhoi, wedi cael ei eni cyn 1 Ionawr 2009, a


(b)naill ai—


(i)bod y cyhuddedig wedi cymryd camau rhesymol i gadarnhau oedran y person hwnnw, neu


(ii)na allai neb fod wedi amau’n rhesymol o olwg y person hwnnw fod y person wedi cael ei eni ar neu ar ôl 1 Ionawr 2009\.


(5\)At ddibenion is\-adran [(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13279)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13286), mae’r cyhuddedig i gael ei drin fel pe bai wedi cymryd camau rhesymol i gadarnhau oedran person—


(a)os gofynnodd y cyhuddedig i’r person hwnnw am dystiolaeth o oedran y person hwnnw, a


(b)pe bai’r dystiolaeth wedi argyhoeddi person rhesymol.


(6\)Pan fo person wedi ei gyhuddo o drosedd o dan yr adran hon oherwydd gweithred neu ddiffyg person arall, neu yn rhinwedd cymhwyso adran 44 o Ddeddf Llysoedd Ynadon [1980 (p.43\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/1980/43) (helpwyr ac anogwyr), mae’n amddiffyniad dangos i’r person gymryd rhagofalon rhesymol ac arfer diwydrwydd dyladwy i osgoi cyflawni’r drosedd.”


Commencement Information

I238Sch. 5 para. 4 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

Prospective

5In the English language text, before section 52 insert—

### “51AOffence of handing over tobacco etc to people born on or after 1 January 2009

(1\)A person (“A”) commits an offence if—


(a)in connection with arrangements under section 53, A hands over in Wales tobacco products, herbal smoking products or cigarette papers to a person born on or after 1 January 2009 (“B”),


(b)the handing over does not take place either—


(i)in the course of B’s trade, profession, business or employment, or


(ii)in the presence of another person who was born before 1 January 2009,


(c)at the time of the handing over, A knows that tobacco products, herbal smoking products or cigarette papers (whichever is the case) are being handed over, and


(d)when handed over, the tobacco products, herbal smoking products or cigarette papers are not contained in a package that—


(i)is sealed, and


(ii)has an address on it, for the purpose of its delivery to that address in accordance with arrangements within section 53\.


(2\)“Package” in [subsection (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13328)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13351) means a package in addition to the original package in which the tobacco products, herbal smoking products or cigarette papers were supplied for the purpose of retail sale by their manufacturer or importer.


(3\)A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.


(4\)Where a person (“the accused”) is charged with an offence under this section by reason of the accused’s own conduct (and otherwise than by virtue of section 44 of the Magistrates’ Courts Act [1980 (c.43\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/1980/43) (aiders and abettors)) it is a defence for the accused to show—


(a)that the accused believed, when the handing over took place, that the person to whom the tobacco products, herbal smoking products or cigarette papers were handed over, or another person present at the time of the handing over, was born before 1 January 2009, and


(b)either—


(i)that the accused had taken reasonable steps to establish the age of that person, or


(ii)that nobody could reasonably have suspected from that person’s appearance that the person was born on or after 1 January 2009\.


(5\)For the purposes of [subsection (4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13374)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p13381), the accused is to be treated as having taken reasonable steps to establish the age of a person if—


(a)the accused asked that person for evidence of that person’s age, and


(b)the evidence would have convinced a reasonable person.


(6\)Where a person is charged with an offence under this section by reason of the act or default of another person, or by virtue of the application of section 44 of the Magistrates’ Courts Act [1980 (c.43\)](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/1980/43) (aiders and abettors), it is a defence to show that the person took reasonable precautions and exercised due diligence to avoid committing the offence.”


Commencement Information

I239Sch. 5 para. 5 not in force at Royal Assent, see [**s. 175(5\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/5)

### “54APower to extend this Chapter to other products

(1\)The Welsh Ministers may by regulations amend this Chapter for the purpose of extending any provision that applies in relation to a tobacco product to—


(a)a device of a specified description which enables a tobacco product to be consumed (for example, a heated tobacco device or pipe);


(b)an item which is intended to form part of such a device.


(2\)Before making regulations under this section the Welsh Ministers must consult any persons the Welsh Ministers consider it appropriate to consult.”

### “55Interpretation of this Chapter

In this Chapter—


<ul><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>cigarette papers</span></span><span>” (“</span><em><span>papurau sigaréts</span></em><span>”) includes anything intended to be used for encasing tobacco products or herbal smoking products for the purpose of enabling them to be smoked;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>employment</span></span><span>” (“</span><em><span>cyflogaeth</span></em><span>”) means any employment, whether paid or unpaid, and includes—</span>
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p><span>work under a contract for services or as an office holder, and</span>
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p><span>work experience provided pursuant to a training course or programme or in the course of training for employment;</span>
</p></div></div></div></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>herbal smoking product</span></span><span>” (“</span><em><span>cynnyrch smygu llysieuol</span></em><span>”) has the meaning given by section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-50"><span>50</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>nicotine product</span></span><span>” (</span><em><span>“cynnyrch nicotin”</span></em><span>) has the meaning given by section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-50"><span>50</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>tobacco product</span></span><span>” (“</span><em><span>cynnyrch tybaco</span></em><span>”) has the meaning given by section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-50"><span>50</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>vaping product</span></span><span>” (“</span><em><span>cynnyrch fepio</span></em><span>”) has the meaning given by section </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#section-50"><span>50</span></a><span> of the Tobacco and Vapes Act 2026.<span>”</span></span>
</p></li></ul>

(a)omit the definition of “nicotine vapour product business”;


(b)in the definition of “tobacco or nicotine vapour product business”, for “nicotine vapour” substitute “vaping” in both places;


(c)at the appropriate places insert—


<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>medical device</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by the Medical Devices Regulations 2002 (</span><a href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/uksi/2002/618"><span>S.I. 2002/618</span></a><span>),<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>medicinal product</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by the Human Medicines Regulations 2012 (</span><a href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/uksi/2012/1916"><span>S.I. 2012/1916</span></a><span>),<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>vape</span></span><span>” means—</span>
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p><span>a device which—</span>
</p><div><div><div><div>(i)</div><p><span>vaporises substances, other than tobacco, for the purpose of inhalation through a mouthpiece (whether or not it also vaporises tobacco), and</span>
</p></div><div><div>(ii)</div><p><span>is not a medical device or a medicinal product, or</span>
</p></div></div></div></div><div><div>(b)</div><p><span>an item which is intended to form part of a device within paragraph (a) (including anything intended to be attached to it with a view to imparting flavour),<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></div></div></div></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>vaping product</span></span><span>” means—</span>
</p><div><div><div><div>(a)</div><p><span>a vape, or</span>
</p></div><div><div>(b)</div><p><span>a vaping substance,<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></div></div></div></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>vaping product business</span></span><span>” means a business involving the sale of vaping products by retail,<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>vaping substance</span></span><span>” means a substance, other than tobacco, that is intended to be vaporised by a vape,<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>vaporises</span></span><span>” includes aerosolises (and “</span><span><span>vaporised</span></span><span>” is to be construed accordingly).<span>”</span></span>
</p></li></ul>

Commencement Information

I309Sch. 8 para. 18 in force at 29\.6\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

19Omit section 35A (meaning of “nicotine vapour product”).

Commencement Information

I310Sch. 8 para. 19 in force at 29\.6\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

### Transitional provision

20In any legislation passed at a time before this Schedule comes into force, and in any instrument or other document made before that time under or for the purposes of the Tobacco and Primary Medical Services (Scotland) Act 2010, any reference to a nicotine vapour product (within the meaning of section 35A of that Act before its repeal by this Schedule) is to be read, in relation to times after this Schedule comes into force, as a reference to a vaping product (within the meaning of section 35 of that Act).


Commencement Information

I311Sch. 8 para. 20 in force at 29\.6\.2026, see [**s. 175(1\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/1)

Section 88(2\)

Schedule 11Retail licensing scheme in Northern Ireland
------------------------------------------------------

Commencement Information

I339Sch. 11 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(8\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/8)

 In the [Tobacco Retailers Act (Northern Ireland) 2014 (c. 4 (N.I.))](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/nia/2014/4/contents), after section 26 insert—


 Section 4A(6\)

### “Schedule 1Retail licensing scheme

#### Introduction

1This Schedule is about the provision that may be made by regulations under [section 4A](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05222)[(4\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05262).


#### Licensing authority

2The regulations must specify a council (a “licensing authority”) which is to grant licences.


#### Grant of licence

3(1\)The regulations may—


(a)prohibit a licensing authority from granting a licence unless satisfied as to a matter specified in the regulations;


(b)require a licensing authority to have regard, in deciding whether to grant a licence, to a matter specified in the regulations.


(2\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p14986)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p14989) includes—


(a)provision prohibiting a licensing authority from granting a premises licence in respect of premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations;


(b)provision limiting the number of licensed premises within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may make provision requiring a licensing authority not to grant a premises licence unless the premises have been inspected in accordance with the regulations.


#### Licence fee

4(1\)The regulations may authorise a licensing authority to charge a fee in respect of an application for the grant of a licence (which may be set at a level that takes into account the cost of exercising functions under or in connection with sections 4A to 4C or the regulations).


(2\)Any such fee must not exceed an amount specified in, or determined in accordance with, the regulations.


(3\)The regulations may make provision for the payment by a licensing authority of a proportion of any amount received by virtue of sub\-paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15021) to any other person with functions under or in connection with sections 4A to 4C or the regulations.


#### Licence conditions

5(1\)The regulations may make provision for the grant of a licence subject to conditions.


(2\)Provision of the kind mentioned in sub\-paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15038) may—


(a)enable a licensing authority to attach conditions to a licence;


(b)require a licensing authority to attach to a licence a condition specified in the regulations.


(3\)The provision that may be made under sub\-paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15038) includes provision prohibiting or restricting the sale of relevant products within an area of a description specified in the regulations.


#### Duration etc of licence

6(1\)The regulations may make provision about the duration, renewal, variation, suspension or revocation of licences.


(2\)The provision that may be made under sub\-paragraph [(1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15064) includes provision conferring power on a court by which a person is convicted of an offence under section 4B to vary, suspend or revoke a licence.


#### Publication of licence information

7The regulations may make provision for the publication by a licensing authority of information relating to licences granted by the licensing authority.


#### Reviews and appeals

8(1\)The regulations must specify the circumstances in which a person may request a review of a decision taken under the regulations.


(2\)The regulations must confer a right of appeal to a magistrates’ court against a decision taken on a review.


(3\)The regulations may contain provision about time limits for requesting reviews or initiating appeals.


#### Guidance

9The regulations may require a licensing authority, in carrying out functions under the regulations, to have regard to guidance published by the Department.


#### Sub\-delegation

10The regulations may confer discretions.


#### Interpretation

11In this Schedule—


<ul><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>grant</span></span><span>” includes vary or renew;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>licence</span></span><span>” means a personal licence or a premises licence;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>licensing authority</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p14979"><span>paragraph 2</span></a><span>;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>personal licence</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05222"><span>section 4A</span></a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05275"><span>(7)</span></a><span>;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>premises licence</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05222"><span>section 4A</span></a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05275"><span>(7)</span></a><span>;</span>
</p></li><li><p><span>“</span><span><span>relevant products</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05222"><span>section 4A</span></a><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05275"><span>(7)</span></a><span>.<span>”</span></span>
</p></li></ul>

 Section 88(3\)

Schedule 12Financial penalties for breach of retail licence conditions in Northern Ireland
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Commencement Information

I340Sch. 12 in force at Royal Assent for specified purposes, see [**s. 175(2\)(8\)**](http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id/ukpga/2026/18/section/175/2/8)

 After [Schedule 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/nia/2014/4/schedule/1) to the [Tobacco Retailers Act (Northern Ireland) 2014 (c. 4 (N.I.))](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/nia/2014/4/contents) (inserted by [Schedule 11](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#schedule-11) to this Act) insert—


 Section 4C(4\)

### “Schedule 2Financial penalties for breach of retail licence conditions

#### Introduction

1This Schedule makes further provision in connection with the imposition of financial penalties under [section 4C](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05417).


#### Notices of intent

2(1\)A council must, before imposing a financial penalty on a person, give the person written notice (a “notice of intent”) of the proposed financial penalty.


(2\)A notice of intent must specify—


(a)the amount of the proposed financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for proposing to impose the penalty,


(c)information about the right to make representations under [paragraph 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15218), and


(d)the date by which any representations must be made.


(3\)The date specified under sub\-paragraph [(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15183)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15199) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the notice of intent is given to the person.


(4\)The council may at any time withdraw the notice of intent, or amend it to reduce the amount of the proposed financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


#### Right to make representations

3(1\)A person who is given a notice of intent under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15178) may make written representations to the council that issued the notice about the proposal to impose a financial penalty.


(2\)Any representations must be made within the period (“the period for representations”) ending with the date specified under [paragraph 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15178)[(2\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15183)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15199).


#### Final notices

4(1\)After the end of the period for representations the council must decide whether to impose a financial penalty on the person.


(2\)If the council decides to impose a financial penalty on the person, the council must give the person written notice (a “final notice”) imposing the penalty.


(3\)A final notice must specify—


(a)the amount of the financial penalty,


(b)the reasons for imposing the penalty,


(c)the date by which the penalty must be paid,


(d)information about the right of appeal under [paragraph 5](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15287), and


(e)the consequence of failure to comply with the final notice.


(4\)The date specified under [sub\-paragraph (3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15244)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15255) must be a date more than 28 days after the day on which the final notice is given to the person.


(5\)The council may at any time withdraw a final notice, or amend it to reduce the amount of the financial penalty, by giving written notice to the person.


(6\)A final notice may not be given more than 28 days after the last day of the period for representations.


#### Appeals

5(1\)A person on whom a financial penalty is imposed under [section 4C](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05417) may appeal to the magistrates’ court against—


(a)the decision to impose the penalty, or


(b)the amount of the penalty.


(2\)An appeal under this paragraph must be brought before the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the day after the day on which the final notice is given to the person in accordance with [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15235).


(3\)On an appeal under this paragraph the magistrates’ court may confirm, reduce or cancel the penalty.


(4\)If a person appeals under this paragraph, the final notice is suspended until the appeal is finally determined, withdrawn or abandoned.


#### Recovery

6(1\)This paragraph applies if a person fails to pay the whole or part of a financial penalty before the end of the period within which the person is required to pay the penalty.


(2\)The council that imposed the financial penalty may recover the unpaid amount of the penalty as if it were payable under an order of a county court.


#### Use of proceeds

7(1\)A council may use any sums it receives in pursuance of final notices given under [paragraph 4](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15235) (its “financial penalty receipts”) only for the purposes of its functions under this Act.


(2\)A council must supply the Department with such information relating to its use of its financial penalty receipts as the Department may require.


(3\)Regulations may make provision for what a council is to do with its financial penalty receipts—


(a)pending their being used for the purposes mentioned in [sub\-paragraph (1\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15330);


(b)if they are not used for those purposes within a period of time specified in the regulations and beginning with their receipt.


(4\)The provision that may be made under [sub\-paragraph (3\)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15339)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p15347) includes (in particular) provision for the payment of sums to a person (including the Department) other than the council.


(5\)Regulations may make provision for accounting arrangements in respect of a council's financial penalty receipts.


(6\)Before making regulations under this paragraph, the Department must consult—


(a)councils, and


(b)such other persons as the Department considers appropriate.”


 Prospective

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>nicotine product</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by Article </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05036"><span>7</span></a><span> of the Health and Personal Social Services (Northern Ireland) Order 1978;<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

(c)for the definition of “tobacco” substitute—


<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>tobacco product</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by Article </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05036"><span>7</span></a><span> of the Health and Personal Social Services (Northern Ireland) Order 1978;<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

(d)in the definition of “tobacco business”, for “tobacco” substitute “tobacco products, herbal smoking products”;


(e)at the appropriate places insert—


<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>cigarette papers</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by Article </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05036"><span>7</span></a><span> of the Health and Personal Social Services (Northern Ireland) Order 1978;<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>filter</span></span><span>” means a filter that is intended to be used when smoking a tobacco product or herbal smoking product (including a filter that forms part of, or that is intended to be inserted into, an item such as a cigarette holder or pipe);<span>”</span>;</span>
</p></li></ul>

<ul><li><p><span><span>“</span>“</span><span><span>herbal smoking product</span></span><span>” has the meaning given by Article </span><a href="https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2026/18/data.xht#p05036"><span>7</span></a><span> of the Health and Personal Social Services (Northern Ireland) Order 1978;<span>”</span>;</span>

(a)the advertising relates to those products in general or to a category of those products, but not to a particular brand, and


(b)the inclusion of the advertising in the service is in accordance with arrangements made by a public authority.
